# Subagent-Driven Development

Execute plan by dispatching fresh subagent per task, with two-stage review after each: spec compliance review first, then code quality review.

**Why subagents:** You delegate tasks to specialized agents with isolated context. By precisely crafting their instructions and context, you ensure they stay focused and succeed at their task. They should never inherit your session's context or history — you construct exactly what they need. This also preserves your own context for coordination work.

**Core principle:** Fresh subagent per task + two-stage review (spec then quality) = high quality, fast iteration

## When to Use

```dot
digraph when_to_use {
    "Have implementation plan?" [shape=diamond];
    "Tasks mostly independent?" [shape=diamond];
    "Stay in this session?" [shape=diamond];
    "subagent-driven-development" [shape=box];
    "executing-plans" [shape=box];
    "Manual execution or brainstorm first" [shape=box];

    "Have implementation plan?" -> "Tasks mostly independent?" [label="yes"];
    "Have implementation plan?" -> "Manual execution or brainstorm first" [label="no"];
    "Tasks mostly independent?" -> "Stay in this session?" [label="yes"];
    "Tasks mostly independent?" -> "Manual execution or brainstorm first" [label="no - tightly coupled"];
    "Stay in this session?" -> "subagent-driven-development" [label="yes"];
    "Stay in this session?" -> "executing-plans" [label="no - parallel session"];
}
```

**vs. Executing Plans (parallel session):**
- Same session (no context switch)
- Fresh subagent per task (no context pollution)
- Two-stage review after each task: spec compliance first, then code quality
- Faster iteration (no human-in-loop between tasks)

## The Process

```dot
digraph process {
    rankdir=TB;

    subgraph cluster_per_task {
        label="Per Task";
        "Dispatch implementer subagent (./implementer-prompt.md)" [shape=box];
        "Implementer subagent asks questions?" [shape=diamond];
        "Answer questions, provide context" [shape=box];
        "Implementer subagent implements, tests, commits, self-reviews" [shape=box];
        "Dispatch spec reviewer subagent (./spec-reviewer-prompt.md)" [shape=box];
        "Spec reviewer subagent confirms code matches spec?" [shape=diamond];
        "Implementer subagent fixes spec gaps" [shape=box];
        "Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent (./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md)" [shape=box];
        "Code quality reviewer subagent approves?" [shape=diamond];
        "Implementer subagent fixes quality issues" [shape=box];
        "Mark task complete in TodoWrite" [shape=box];
    }

    "Read plan, extract all tasks with full text, note context, create TodoWrite" [shape=box];
    "More tasks remain?" [shape=diamond];
    "Dispatch final code reviewer subagent for entire implementation" [shape=box];
    "Use superpowers:finishing-a-development-branch" [shape=box style=filled fillcolor=lightgreen];

    "Read plan, extract all tasks with full text, note context, create TodoWrite" -> "Dispatch implementer subagent (./implementer-prompt.md)";
    "Dispatch implementer subagent (./implementer-prompt.md)" -> "Implementer subagent asks questions?";
    "Implementer subagent asks questions?" -> "Answer questions, provide context" [label="yes"];
    "Answer questions, provide context" -> "Dispatch implementer subagent (./implementer-prompt.md)";
    "Implementer subagent asks questions?" -> "Implementer subagent implements, tests, commits, self-reviews" [label="no"];
    "Implementer subagent implements, tests, commits, self-reviews" -> "Dispatch spec reviewer subagent (./spec-reviewer-prompt.md)";
    "Dispatch spec reviewer subagent (./spec-reviewer-prompt.md)" -> "Spec reviewer subagent confirms code matches spec?";
    "Spec reviewer subagent confirms code matches spec?" -> "Implementer subagent fixes spec gaps" [label="no"];
    "Implementer subagent fixes spec gaps" -> "Dispatch spec reviewer subagent (./spec-reviewer-prompt.md)" [label="re-review"];
    "Spec reviewer subagent confirms code matches spec?" -> "Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent (./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md)" [label="yes"];
    "Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent (./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md)" -> "Code quality reviewer subagent approves?";
    "Code quality reviewer subagent approves?" -> "Implementer subagent fixes quality issues" [label="no"];
    "Implementer subagent fixes quality issues" -> "Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent (./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md)" [label="re-review"];
    "Code quality reviewer subagent approves?" -> "Mark task complete in TodoWrite" [label="yes"];
    "Mark task complete in TodoWrite" -> "More tasks remain?";
    "More tasks remain?" -> "Dispatch implementer subagent (./implementer-prompt.md)" [label="yes"];
    "More tasks remain?" -> "Dispatch final code reviewer subagent for entire implementation" [label="no"];
    "Dispatch final code reviewer subagent for entire implementation" -> "Use superpowers:finishing-a-development-branch";
}
```

## Model Selection

Use the least powerful model that can handle each role to conserve cost and increase speed.

**Mechanical implementation tasks** (isolated functions, clear specs, 1-2 files): use a fast, cheap model. Most implementation tasks are mechanical when the plan is well-specified.

**Integration and judgment tasks** (multi-file coordination, pattern matching, debugging): use a standard model.

**Architecture, design, and review tasks**: use the most capable available model.

**Task complexity signals:**
- Touches 1-2 files with a complete spec → cheap model
- Touches multiple files with integration concerns → standard model
- Requires design judgment or broad codebase understanding → most capable model

## Handling Implementer Status

Implementer subagents report one of four statuses. Handle each appropriately:

**DONE:** Proceed to spec compliance review.

**DONE_WITH_CONCERNS:** The implementer completed the work but flagged doubts. Read the concerns before proceeding. If the concerns are about correctness or scope, address them before review. If they're observations (e.g., "this file is getting large"), note them and proceed to review.

**NEEDS_CONTEXT:** The implementer needs information that wasn't provided. Provide the missing context and re-dispatch.

**BLOCKED:** The implementer cannot complete the task. Assess the blocker:
1. If it's a context problem, provide more context and re-dispatch with the same model
2. If the task requires more reasoning, re-dispatch with a more capable model
3. If the task is too large, break it into smaller pieces
4. If the plan itself is wrong, escalate to the human

**Never** ignore an escalation or force the same model to retry without changes. If the implementer said it's stuck, something needs to change.

## Prompt Templates

- `./implementer-prompt.md` - Dispatch implementer subagent
- `./spec-reviewer-prompt.md` - Dispatch spec compliance reviewer subagent
- `./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md` - Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent

## Example Workflow

```
You: I'm using Subagent-Driven Development to execute this plan.

[Read plan file once: docs/superpowers/plans/feature-plan.md]
[Extract all 5 tasks with full text and context]
[Create TodoWrite with all tasks]

Task 1: Hook installation script

[Get Task 1 text and context (already extracted)]
[Dispatch implementation subagent with full task text + context]

Implementer: "Before I begin - should the hook be installed at user or system level?"

You: "User level (~/.config/superpowers/hooks/)"

Implementer: "Got it. Implementing now..."
[Later] Implementer:
  - Implemented install-hook command
  - Added tests, 5/5 passing
  - Self-review: Found I missed --force flag, added it
  - Committed

[Dispatch spec compliance reviewer]
Spec reviewer: ✅ Spec compliant - all requirements met, nothing extra

[Get git SHAs, dispatch code quality reviewer]
Code reviewer: Strengths: Good test coverage, clean. Issues: None. Approved.

[Mark Task 1 complete]

Task 2: Recovery modes

[Get Task 2 text and context (already extracted)]
[Dispatch implementation subagent with full task text + context]

Implementer: [No questions, proceeds]
Implementer:
  - Added verify/repair modes
  - 8/8 tests passing
  - Self-review: All good
  - Committed

[Dispatch spec compliance reviewer]
Spec reviewer: ❌ Issues:
  - Missing: Progress reporting (spec says "report every 100 items")
  - Extra: Added --json flag (not requested)

[Implementer fixes issues]
Implementer: Removed --json flag, added progress reporting

[Spec reviewer reviews again]
Spec reviewer: ✅ Spec compliant now

[Dispatch code quality reviewer]
Code reviewer: Strengths: Solid. Issues (Important): Magic number (100)

[Implementer fixes]
Implementer: Extracted PROGRESS_INTERVAL constant

[Code reviewer reviews again]
Code reviewer: ✅ Approved

[Mark Task 2 complete]

...

[After all tasks]
[Dispatch final code-reviewer]
Final reviewer: All requirements met, ready to merge

Done!
```

## Advantages

**vs. Manual execution:**
- Subagents follow TDD naturally
- Fresh context per task (no confusion)
- Parallel-safe (subagents don't interfere)
- Subagent can ask questions (before AND during work)

**vs. Executing Plans:**
- Same session (no handoff)
- Continuous progress (no waiting)
- Review checkpoints automatic

**Efficiency gains:**
- No file reading overhead (controller provides full text)
- Controller curates exactly what context is needed
- Subagent gets complete information upfront
- Questions surfaced before work begins (not after)

**Quality gates:**
- Self-review catches issues before handoff
- Two-stage review: spec compliance, then code quality
- Review loops ensure fixes actually work
- Spec compliance prevents over/under-building
- Code quality ensures implementation is well-built

**Cost:**
- More subagent invocations (implementer + 2 reviewers per task)
- Controller does more prep work (extracting all tasks upfront)
- Review loops add iterations
- But catches issues early (cheaper than debugging later)

## Red Flags

**Never:**
- Start implementation on main/master branch without explicit user consent
- Skip reviews (spec compliance OR code quality)
- Proceed with unfixed issues
- Dispatch multiple implementation subagents in parallel (conflicts)
- Make subagent read plan file (provide full text instead)
- Skip scene-setting context (subagent needs to understand where task fits)
- Ignore subagent questions (answer before letting them proceed)
- Accept "close enough" on spec compliance (spec reviewer found issues = not done)
- Skip review loops (reviewer found issues = implementer fixes = review again)
- Let implementer self-review replace actual review (both are needed)
- **Start code quality review before spec compliance is ✅** (wrong order)
- Move to next task while either review has open issues

**If subagent asks questions:**
- Answer clearly and completely
- Provide additional context if needed
- Don't rush them into implementation

**If reviewer finds issues:**
- Implementer (same subagent) fixes them
- Reviewer reviews again
- Repeat until approved
- Don't skip the re-review

**If subagent fails task:**
- Dispatch fix subagent with specific instructions
- Don't try to fix manually (context pollution)

## Integration

**Required workflow skills:**
- **superpowers:using-git-worktrees** - REQUIRED: Set up isolated workspace before starting
- **superpowers:writing-plans** - Creates the plan this skill executes
- **superpowers:requesting-code-review** - Code review template for reviewer subagents
- **superpowers:finishing-a-development-branch** - Complete development after all tasks

**Subagents should use:**
- **superpowers:test-driven-development** - Subagents follow TDD for each task

**Alternative workflow:**
- **superpowers:executing-plans** - Use for parallel session instead of same-session execution

# Validate smol

Run all automated checks for the smol flight controller. Activate `~/.venvs/smol` before every command.

**CRITICAL**: Capture the FULL output of every command. Never re-run a command just to see which tests failed — read the output you already have. Use `2>&1` to merge stderr, and save long outputs to a file if needed.

## Checks

Run these in order. If a check fails, stop and report — do not continue to later checks.

### 1. Regenerate and format

Regenerate all generated files and run the formatter. This ensures we never commit stale generated code or unformatted source.

```bash
python3 protocol/generate.py && just format && just check-format && just check-codegen
```

Both checks must pass. Generated files (`src/protocol/`) are excluded from formatting — the generator owns their style.

### 2. Native unit tests

```bash
just test-native 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-native.txt
```

Read the FULL output to find failures. Do NOT re-run just to see which tests failed.

Report pass/fail count from the summary line (e.g., "118 test cases: 118 succeeded").

Known flaky: `test_smol_matches_full_after_full_sequence` (BUG-006, FullEkf nondeterminism). If ONLY this test fails, re-run once. If it fails twice, report it.

### 3. Thread sanitizer

```bash
just test-tsan 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-tsan.txt
```

Catches data races in SharedState, ring buffer, and cross-thread communication. Requires `setarch -R` for ASLR compatibility on Linux 6.x.

### 4. Elixir GCS tests

```bash
just test-gcs 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-gcs.txt
```

### 5. Native build

```bash
just build-native
```

### 6. RP2350B build (CMake)

```bash
just build-fc3
```

This catches missing source files in `CMakeLists.txt` and RP2350B-specific compilation errors that native builds miss.

### 7. Replay validation

```bash
just test-replay 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-replay.txt
```

This builds `native_full_ekf`, replays reference flight data through both EKFs, and checks RMS error bounds vs truth. Requires steps 4-5 to have passed.

## Report

```
## Validation Report

### Regenerate + format
[PASS — tree clean / PASS — N files updated / FAIL — details]

### Native tests
[PASS — N test cases: N succeeded / FAIL — details]

### Thread sanitizer
[PASS / FAIL — details]

### GCS tests
[PASS — N tests: N passed / FAIL — details]

### Native build
[PASS / FAIL]

### RP2350B build
[PASS / FAIL — details if failed]

### Replay validation
[PASS — N passed / FAIL — details]

### Summary
[READY TO SHIP / NEEDS FIXES — list what failed]
```

- Failures: fix and re-run `/validate-smol`

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

# Code Review

Review all changes on the current branch against main.

## Process

### 1. Gather Changes

```bash
git diff main --name-only
```

If no changes, inform the user and stop.

For each changed file, read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand context. Also run:

```bash
git diff main
```

### 2. Review Against Guidelines

#### Code Reads Like Prose
- Descriptive function and variable names — no abbreviations that require mental decoding
- Linear data flows — can you read top-to-bottom without jumping around?
- Efficient line count — no bloat, no unnecessary abstractions
- DRY — is anything duplicated that shouldn't be?
- Single responsibility — each function does ONE thing, each class has ONE purpose
- Testable — could you write a test for this without mocking half the system?

#### Make Invalid States Unrepresentable
- Constraints encoded in types, not runtime checks
- No scattered validation for the same invariant
- `std::optional`, enums, and constructors used to enforce validity

#### Trace the Data
- Where does each value come from? What constraints does it carry?
- Are there redundant conversions or unnecessary intermediates?
- Does every downstream consumer get what it expects?

#### Always Make It Better
- Did we touch code without improving it?
- Are there obvious improvements just outside the diff boundary? (note in suggestions, don't block)

#### Project Conventions (from CLAUDE.md)
- No docstrings unless asked
- No fallbacks — code works or fails loudly
- No dead code, no commented-out experiments
- No default arguments
- Leading underscores for class data members
- PascalCase functions, snake_case locals, kCamelCase constants
- "latest" not "last" for most recent values
- Parameter passing: pointer for mutation, const ref for read-only, const value for scalars

### 3. Check For Slop
- Comments that explain "what" instead of "why"
- Defensive checks for conditions that can't happen
- Unnecessary try/catch or error handling beyond system boundaries
- Verbose logging that doesn't match existing patterns
- Style inconsistencies with surrounding code

### 4. Present Results

```
## Review Summary

**Assessment**: [APPROVE / REQUEST CHANGES]

### Positive Findings
- What was done well

### Required Changes
- Issues that must be fixed (file:line references)

### Suggestions
- Optional improvements

### Convention Violations
- Any CLAUDE.md or guideline violations
```

Be specific with file:line references. Prioritize correctness and readability over micro-optimizations. If approved, suggest running `/validate-smol` next.

# Validate smol

Run all automated checks for the smol flight controller. Activate `~/.venvs/smol` before every command.

**CRITICAL**: Capture the FULL output of every command. Never re-run a command just to see which tests failed — read the output you already have. Use `2>&1` to merge stderr, and save long outputs to a file if needed.

## Checks

Run these in order. If a check fails, stop and report — do not continue to later checks.

### 1. Regenerate and format

Regenerate all generated files and run the formatter. This ensures we never commit stale generated code or unformatted source.

```bash
python3 protocol/generate.py && just format && just check-format && just check-codegen && just check-include-boundary
```

All four checks must pass. Generated files (`src/protocol/`) are excluded from formatting — the generator owns their style. `check-include-boundary` enforces ADR-C C-1 (fast-loop paths must not include from `src/mission/`).

### 2. Native unit tests

```bash
just test-native 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-native.txt
```

Read the FULL output to find failures. Do NOT re-run just to see which tests failed.

Report pass/fail count from the summary line (e.g., "118 test cases: 118 succeeded").

Known flaky: `test_smol_matches_full_after_full_sequence` (BUG-006, FullEkf nondeterminism). If ONLY this test fails, re-run once. If it fails twice, report it.

### 3. Thread sanitizer

```bash
just test-tsan 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-tsan.txt
```

Catches data races in SharedState, ring buffer, and cross-thread communication. Requires `setarch -R` for ASLR compatibility on Linux 6.x.

### 4. Elixir GCS tests

```bash
just test-gcs 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-gcs.txt
```

### 5. Native build

```bash
just build-native
```

### 6. RP2350B build (CMake)

```bash
just build-fc3
```

This catches missing source files in `CMakeLists.txt` and RP2350B-specific compilation errors that native builds miss.

### 7. Replay validation

```bash
just test-replay 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-replay.txt
```

This builds `native_full_ekf`, replays reference flight data through both EKFs, and checks RMS error bounds vs truth. Requires steps 4-5 to have passed.

## Report

```
## Validation Report

### Regenerate + format + include-boundary
[PASS — tree clean / PASS — N files updated / FAIL — details]

### Native tests
[PASS — N test cases: N succeeded / FAIL — details]

### Thread sanitizer
[PASS / FAIL — details]

### GCS tests
[PASS — N tests: N passed / FAIL — details]

### Native build
[PASS / FAIL]

### RP2350B build
[PASS / FAIL — details if failed]

### Replay validation
[PASS — N passed / FAIL — details]

### Summary
[READY TO SHIP / NEEDS FIXES — list what failed]
```

## Next Steps

- All pass: `/ship` to commit
- Failures: fix and re-run `/validate-smol`

# Ship PR

Create a feature branch from the current branch, commit all changes, push, and open a PR.

## Pre-flight

Verify we have changes to ship:

```bash
git status
git diff --stat
git diff --cached --stat
```

If there are no changes (staged or unstaged, tracked or untracked), stop and inform the user.

## Gather Context

```bash
git branch --show-current
git log --oneline -5
```

The current branch becomes the PR's **base branch** (the branch to merge into). If already on a feature branch, ask the user if they want to PR into the branch they branched from instead.

## Steps

### 1. Determine branch name and commit message

If the user provided arguments, use them to derive:
- **Branch name**: kebab-case, prefixed with `feat/`, `fix/`, or `refactor/` based on the change type. Max 50 chars.
- **Commit message**: conventional commit format from the same description.

If no arguments provided, analyze the diff to determine both:
- Read `git diff` and `git diff --cached` and any untracked files
- Classify the change (feat, fix, refactor, docs, test, chore)
- Draft a branch name and commit message

**Show the user the proposed branch name and commit message before proceeding.** Wait for approval.

### 2. Create branch and commit

```bash
git checkout -b <branch-name>
```

Stage all relevant files. **Do NOT stage:**
- `.env` files or credentials
- Large binary files unless they're clearly intentional (e.g., `.uf2` firmware)

```bash
git add <specific files>
git commit -m "<message>

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>"
```

Use a HEREDOC for multi-line commit messages.

### 3. Push

```bash
git push -u origin <branch-name>
```

### 4. Create PR

```bash
gh pr create --base <base-branch> --title "<title>" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Summary
<1-3 bullet points describing the changes>

## Test plan
<How the changes were validated>


🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)
EOF
)"
```

The PR body should summarize what changed and how it was tested. Reference any validation output if `/validate-smol` or similar was run.

### 5. Report

```
PR created: <url>
Branch: <branch-name> → <base-branch>
```

## Safety Rules

- **Never force push**
- **Never push to main/master directly** — always create a branch
- **Always show the branch name and commit message before creating them**
- **If the user is already on a feature branch with commits**, ask whether to create a new branch or use the current one
- Stage files explicitly — never use `git add -A` or `git add .`

# Backlog Mode

You are in **Backlog Mode** - documenting bugs and improvements WITHOUT implementing them.

**Reference skills based on issue domain:**
- API issues: Read `.claude/skills/api-design-patterns/SKILL.md`
- Frontend components: Read `.claude/skills/react-patterns/SKILL.md`
- Error handling: Read `.claude/skills/error-handler/SKILL.md`
- UX improvements: Read `.claude/skills/frontend-design/SKILL.md`

## Available Tools & When to Use Them

### Codebase Exploration
Use **Task tool with Explore subagent** for:
- Finding root causes of bugs
- Understanding current implementation
- Locating affected files and components
```
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Very thorough: find all code related to [X]")
```

### External Research
Use **Exa search** (`mcp__exa__exa_search`) for:
- Checking if others encountered the same bug
- Finding known fixes or workarounds
- Researching UI/UX best practices for similar features
```
mcp__exa__exa_search(query="[framework] [issue description] fix")
```

Use **Ref documentation** (`mcp__Ref__*`) for:
- Checking official framework/library docs
- Verifying correct API usage
- Finding recommended patterns
```
mcp__Ref__ref_search_documentation(query="[library] [feature] documentation")
```

### UI/UX Verification
Use **Playwright** (`mcp__playwright__*`) for UX issues:
- Navigate to the affected page
- Take screenshot of current state (for BACKLOG entry)
- Verify the issue exists as user described
- Document "before" state
```
mcp__playwright__browser_navigate(url="http://localhost:3000/path")
mcp__playwright__browser_take_screenshot(filename="backlog-ux-xxx-before.png")
```

### Complex Analysis
Use **Sequential thinking** (`mcp__sequential-thinking__sequentialthinking`) for:
- Multi-step root cause analysis
- Weighing multiple potential causes
- Structuring complex investigations

---

## Parallel Execution Strategy

You CAN run multiple subagents AND tools in parallel by making multiple tool calls in a single message. Use this for efficiency when tasks are **independent**.

### Multiple Subagents in Parallel

**When to use:**
- Bug/feature spans frontend + backend (separate concerns)
- Investigation touches multiple packages
- Need both code exploration AND documentation research
- Complex issue benefits from divide-and-conquer

**Example - Bug spanning layers:**
```
[Single message, multiple Task calls - all run simultaneously:]

Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Very thorough: find tRPC handlers for [feature]")
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Very thorough: find React components rendering [feature]")
Task(subagent_type="documentation-researcher", prompt="Research [framework] best practices for [pattern]")
```

**Example - Multi-package investigation:**
```
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Search packages/trpc for [issue]")
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Search packages/features for [issue]")
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Search apps/web for [issue]")
```

### Subagents + Tools in Parallel

**Example - UX issue (all at once):**
```
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Find component code for [element]")
mcp__playwright__browser_navigate(url="http://localhost:3000/path")
mcp__exa__exa_search(query="UX best practices [pattern]")
```

### When to Stay Sequential

- Results from first search inform what to search next
- Need to confirm issue exists before deep diving
- Small codebase where one Explore is sufficient
- Risk of overlapping/duplicated search areas

**Example - Sequential dependency:**
```
1. First: Explore → discovers it's a Prisma schema issue
2. Then: Ref search → "Prisma relations documentation"
   (wouldn't know to search Prisma without step 1)
```

### Rule of Thumb
| Situation | Approach |
|-----------|----------|
| Know what to search for | **Parallel** - maximize speed |
| Need to discover what to search | **Sequential** - learn first |
| Large codebase, clear separation | **Parallel subagents** - divide and conquer |
| Small codebase or focused issue | **Single subagent** - avoid overhead |

## Workflow Loop

For each item, execute these steps IN ORDER:

### Step 1: Receive
- Accept ONE item at a time
- If user provides multiple, say: "Let's start with the first one. What is it?"
- If `Yes, add that to the backlog. that test overhead is unacceptable. it's destroying our fast-paced workflow` provided, use that as the item

### Step 2: Classify
Determine type based on description:
| Type | Criteria |
|------|----------|
| **BUG** | Something broken, error, unexpected behavior |
| **ENH** | New feature, capability, or functional improvement |
| **UX** | Visual, usability, or interface improvement |

State your classification: "This sounds like a **[TYPE]**."

### Step 3: Check Duplicates
- Read BACKLOG.md
- Search for similar existing entries
- If potential duplicate found: "This might be related to [ID]. Is this the same issue or different?"

### Step 4: Investigate (Use Appropriate Tools)

**For ALL types:**
- Use **Explore subagent** to find relevant code

**For BUGs additionally:**
- Use **Exa** to search if others hit this issue
- Check for known fixes or workarounds

**For ENH additionally:**
- Use **Ref** to check official docs for best practices
- Use **Exa** to research how others implement similar features

**For UX additionally:**
- Use **Playwright** to navigate to the page and take a screenshot
- Verify the issue exists as described
- Save screenshot as `backlog-ux-XXX-current.png` for documentation

### Step 5: Analyze
Use sequential thinking if complex. Summarize:
- What you found in codebase
- What external research revealed (if any)
- Root cause (BUG) or approach (ENH/UX)
- All affected files with full paths
- Suggested priority (P1/P2/P3)

### Step 6: Preview Entry
Show the complete BACKLOG entry to user:
```
Here's the proposed entry:

### [TYPE-XXX] Title
- **Reported**: date
- **Status**: Open
...

Does this look accurate? Any changes?
```

### Step 7: Document
After user confirms (or says "looks good", "yes", "ok"):
- Add entry to appropriate section in BACKLOG.md
- Update Statistics section
- Confirm: "Added as **[TYPE-XXX]** to BACKLOG.md"

### Step 8: Next Item
Ask: "Next item? (or 'done' to exit backlog mode)"
- If user provides another item → Go to Step 1
- If user says "done", "exit", "that's all" → End with summary of items added

2. **NO CODE CHANGES** - Only read/explore, write only to BACKLOG.md

|----------|----------|

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user's original request was to "continue with the phase 2 tasks" for the smol flight controller (starting from main after PR #76 was merged). This involved implementing Chunk 3 of the mission-graph Phase 2 plan (Tasks 3.5–3.13), which covers the fast-loop side of the slow-loop integration: hold-contract for primary commands, staleness detection, ADR-F response (Tier 1 trigger), SafetyMonitor's kSlowLoopStale case, pre-arm check, task wire-up, end-to-end tests, and validation.
   
   After implementation, the user invoked `/cadre:slop` to remove AI-generated comment slop, then `/cp-review` for code review. Review findings led to explicit user instructions:
   - Fix flight_snapshot_queue capacity (2→8)
   - Unify Clock::ElapsedMs() to one call per tick, threaded through BuildSnapshot where it converts to elapsed_us for PackTiming
   - Fix extern WorldProgress placement
   - Add a note about file-scope singleton state since not being fixed now
   
   Then `/ship-pr` to open a PR, and `/cadre:backlog` to document the test-runtime overhead issue ("test overhead is unacceptable. it's destroying our fast-paced workflow"). User finalized with "done".

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Architecture Decision Records (ADR-A, B, C, F, G) for smol mission-graph
   - Cross-loop comm via `etl::queue_spsc_atomic<T, N>` + drain-to-latest (ADR-A)
   - FreeRTOS dual-core on RP2350B; std::atomic<T> doesn't propagate across Non-shareable SRAM
   - ADR-F fixed thresholds: kSlowLoopStaleThresholdMs=150, kSlowLoopHoldSec=1.0, kSlowLoopBootstrapHoldSec=0.2, kTier1AnchorMaxAgeMs=2000
   - Watchdog class (pure consumer, no transport, no singleton)
   - Transport vs interpretation separation (queue = transport, class = interpretation)
   - Producer:consumer ratio and queue capacity (100Hz fast-loop producer, 20Hz slow-loop consumer → needs capacity ≥5)
   - PlatformIO test framework (per-directory-binary model with test_build_src=yes)
   - Google Test with --gtest_filter for targeted runs
   - Include-boundary enforcement (ADR-C C-1: fast-loop cannot include from src/mission/)

3. Files and Code Sections:
   - **src/core/skill_command.h**
     - Added `using PrimaryControlVariant = std::variant<PlannedLeg, PrimaryControl, std::monostate>;` typedef
     - SkillCommand.primary uses this typedef
   
   - **src/core/flight_loop.h**
     - Added: PollSkillCommand(), PollSlowLoopHeartbeat(), EvaluateSlowLoopResponse(), LatestPrimary(), HasPrimary(), SlowLoopOk(now_ms), SlowLoopStaleTriggered()
     - Added members: _latest_primary, _have_primary, _slow_loop_watchdog, _stale_since_ms, _slow_loop_stale_triggered
     - Changed RunSafetyPipeline and BuildSnapshot signatures to take `const uint32_t now_ms`
   
   - **src/core/flight_loop.cpp**
     - Added `etl::queue_spsc_atomic<FlightSnapshot, 8> flight_snapshot_queue;` (after review: was 2)
     - PollSkillCommand: drain loop with hold-on-non-monostate semantics
     - EvaluateSlowLoopResponse: hold-then-trigger logic
     - Step(): captures `const uint32_t now_ms = Clock::ElapsedMs();` once after Clock::Update(), threads to all consumers
     - BuildSnapshot now calls `PackTiming(&snapshot, timing, static_cast<float>(now_ms) * 1000.0f);`
   
   - **src/core/flight_snapshot.h** (new)
     - FlightSnapshot struct {state, sensors, airspeed_mps, mode, now_ms}
     - extern queue declared with capacity 8
   
   - **src/core/slow_loop_heartbeat.h**
     - Added kSlowLoopHoldSec=1.0f, kSlowLoopBootstrapHoldSec=0.2f, kTier1AnchorMaxAgeMs=2000 (moved from slow_loop.h)

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

# Code Review

Review all changes on the current branch against main.

## Process

### 1. Gather Changes

```bash
git diff main --name-only
```

If no changes, inform the user and stop.

For each changed file, read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand context. Also run:

```bash
git diff main
```

### 2. Review Against Guidelines

#### Code Reads Like Prose
- Descriptive function and variable names — no abbreviations that require mental decoding
- Linear data flows — can you read top-to-bottom without jumping around?
- Efficient line count — no bloat, no unnecessary abstractions
- DRY — is anything duplicated that shouldn't be?
- Single responsibility — each function does ONE thing, each class has ONE purpose
- Testable — could you write a test for this without mocking half the system?

#### Make Invalid States Unrepresentable
- Constraints encoded in types, not runtime checks
- No scattered validation for the same invariant
- `std::optional`, enums, and constructors used to enforce validity

#### Trace the Data
- Where does each value come from? What constraints does it carry?
- Are there redundant conversions or unnecessary intermediates?
- Does every downstream consumer get what it expects?

#### Always Make It Better
- Did we touch code without improving it?
- Are there obvious improvements just outside the diff boundary? (note in suggestions, don't block)

#### Project Conventions (from CLAUDE.md)
- No docstrings unless asked
- No fallbacks — code works or fails loudly
- No dead code, no commented-out experiments
- No default arguments
- Leading underscores for class data members
- PascalCase functions, snake_case locals, kCamelCase constants
- "latest" not "last" for most recent values
- Parameter passing: pointer for mutation, const ref for read-only, const value for scalars

### 3. Check For Slop
- Comments that explain "what" instead of "why"
- Defensive checks for conditions that can't happen
- Unnecessary try/catch or error handling beyond system boundaries
- Verbose logging that doesn't match existing patterns
- Style inconsistencies with surrounding code

### 4. Present Results

```
## Review Summary

**Assessment**: [APPROVE / REQUEST CHANGES]

### Positive Findings
- What was done well

### Required Changes
- Issues that must be fixed (file:line references)

### Suggestions
- Optional improvements

### Convention Violations
- Any CLAUDE.md or guideline violations
```

Be specific with file:line references. Prioritize correctness and readability over micro-optimizations. If approved, suggest running `/validate-smol` next.


ARGUMENTS: Review ALL of our changes to main

2. fix
3. fix\.

2. Key Technical Concepts:

   - Wire-format codegen via protocol/generate.py producing C++/Elixir/Python from TOML
   - etl::queue_spsc_atomic cross-core drain-to-latest (ADR-A)
   - RP2350B dual-core, Non-shareable SRAM (std::atomic does not propagate cross-core)
   - Clock source ambiguity: wall clock (live), simulated flight time (replay/SIL), synthetic cycle_count (native)
   - HAL pattern: link-time polymorphism via hal:: free-function namespace
   - CycleTimer per-cycle state vs Clock current-time-only
   - AdvanceSyntheticCycle: native-only explicit cycle boundary operation
   - ADR-F fixed safety thresholds (kSlowLoopStaleThresholdMs=150, kSlowLoopHoldSec=1.0, kSlowLoopBootstrapHoldSec=0.2, kTier1AnchorMaxAgeMs=2000)
   - Altitude reference frame naming convention (memory rule)
   - No fallbacks rule (code works or fails loudly)
   - No scaffolding ahead of consumers rule

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - **src/hal/clock_hal.h** (NEW):
     - HAL contract: 4 free functions in hal::clock namespace
     - Init(), AdvanceSyntheticCycle(), NowTickUs(), NowWallUs()
     - Contains table mapping HAL → tick source semantics
     - Native non-replay: cycle_count * kCycleBudgetUs
     - RP2350B live: to_us_since_boot
     - Replay: replay packet timestamp
     - SIL: integrator time

   - **src/platform/clock.h** (REWRITTEN):
     - Static class, "what time is it right now?" only
     - Init(), NowUs/NowMs/NowSec (tick µs since Init)
     - NowWallUs (live wall, returns 0 on HALs without wall clock)
     - SetUtcReference/HasUtc/UtcSec (UTC anchor)
     - SetNowUsForTest (test-only, does NOT affect NowWallUs)

   - **src/platform/clock.cpp** (NEW):
     - Forwards NowUs/NowWallUs to hal::clock, subtracts init offset
     - Holds UTC anchor state
     - SetNowUsForTest sets override; Clock::Init clears it

   - **src/platform/cycle_timer.h** (NEW):
     ```cpp
     class CycleTimer {
      public:
       void BeginCycle() {
         hal::clock::AdvanceSyntheticCycle();
         _prev_tick_us = _tick_us;
         _tick_us = Clock::NowUs();
         _cycle_start_wall_us = Clock::NowWallUs();
       }
       uint32_t TickUs()/TickMs()/TickSec() const;
       uint32_t TickDtUs()/TickDtSec() const { return _tick_us - _prev_tick_us; }
       uint32_t CycleBusyUs() const;  // live wall µs since BeginCycle, 0 on no-wall HALs
      private:
       uint32_t _prev_tick_us = 0, _tick_us = 0, _cycle_start_wall_us = 0;
     };
     ```

   - **src/core/flight_loop.h/.cpp**:
     - FlightLoop owns CycleTimer _cycle_timer
     - Exposes CycleBusyUs() passthrough
     - Step() calls `_cycle_timer.BeginCycle()` at top, then reads `TickMs()` for current_elapsed_ms and `TickDtSec()` for dt_sec
     - ComputeControlOutput takes `dt_sec` parameter (was `kFlightLoopIntervalSec`)
     - RunSafetyPipeline takes current_elapsed_ms only (dt_sec removed per review)

   - **src/control/failsafe_responder.{h,cpp}**:
     - Removed unused `dt_s` parameter per review #5
     - Signature: `(verdict, passthrough, nav, safety_mirror, current_elapsed_ms)`
     - CapturePose struct uses `altitude_above_origin_m` field name

   - **src/core/safety_state.h**:
     - `tier1_anchor_altitude_msl_m` renamed to `tier1_anchor_altitude_above_origin_m`

   - **src/mission/world_progress.h**:
     - `center_altitude_msl_m` renamed to `center_altitude_above_origin_m`

   - **src/estimation/airborne.h**:
     - Removed `<cmath>` include
     - Added `kAirborneGroundspeedThresholdSqMps2` constant
     - `IsAirborne` uses squared comparison: `(vn*vn + ve*ve) > threshold_sq`

   - **src/hal/native/hal_native.cpp**:
     - Added `namespace hal::clock { Init, AdvanceSyntheticCycle, NowTickUs, NowWallUs }`
     - AdvanceSyntheticCycle does `if (!replay_mode) cycle_count++;`
     - Removed `cycle_count++` from ReadImu
     - NowWallUs returns 0

   - **src/hal/native/hal_native_sil.cpp**:
     - hal::clock namespace with AdvanceSyntheticCycle() no-op, NowWallUs returns 0

   - **src/hal/rp2350b/hal_rp2350b_live.cpp**:
     - hal::clock namespace; NowTickUs/NowWallUs both return to_us_since_boot; AdvanceSyntheticCycle no-op

   - **src/hal/rp2350b/hal_rp2350b_replay.cpp**:
     - hal::clock namespace; NowTickUs returns replay packet time; NowWallUs returns wall; AdvanceSyntheticCycle no-op
     - Removed static `_cycle_start_wall_us` (obsolete)

   - **src/main_rp2350b_replay.cpp**:
     - Overrun check: `if (_flight_loop.CycleBusyUs() > kCycleBudgetUs)`

   - **protocol/snapshot.toml**:
     - Field renamed: `cycle_us:float32` → `cycle_duration_us:uint32`
     - Protocol hash changed from 0xBADF00 to 0x58D3E2
     - Regenerated src/protocol/snapshot.h, snapshot_decoder.ex, validation/snapshot.py

   - **src/protocol/snapshot_pack.h**: PackTiming takes `uint32_t cycle_duration_us`

   - **src/platform/lap_timer.h**: Uses `Clock::NowWallUs()` instead of CycleElapsedUs

   - **src/platform/watchdog.h**: Renamed `now_ms` → `current_elapsed_ms` in IsStale/TimeSinceLastFeed

   - **src/core/flight_snapshot.h**: Field `now_ms` → `current_elapsed_ms`

   - **src/mission/slow_loop.h, pre_arm.h**: Renamed now_ms → current_elapsed_ms in structs

   - **src/mission/slow_loop_input_builder.cpp**: Uses Clock::NowMs()

   - **tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/timing_analyzer.ex**: Uses `cycle_duration_us` field
   - **tools/smol_gcs/test/timing_analyzer_test.exs**: Tests use integer cycle_duration_us
   - **tools/analyze_timing.py**: Uses `cycle_duration_us` field

   - **test/test_platform/test_platform.cpp**: Added 4 CycleTimer tests
     ```cpp
     TEST(CycleTimerTest, TickDtIsZeroBeforeFirstBeginCycle)
     TEST(CycleTimerTest, FirstBeginCycleCapturesTick)
     TEST(CycleTimerTest, TickDtReflectsDeltaBetweenCycles)
     TEST(CycleTimerTest, TickSnapshotIsConstantWithinCycle)
     ```
     SetElapsedUsForTest renamed to SetNowUsForTest (10 occurrences)

   - **test/test_failsafe_responder/test_failsafe_responder.cpp**: Removed 0.01f dt_s arg from all ComputeFailsafeResponse calls via `perl -i -0pe 's/(\w+,\s+)0\.01f,/$1/g'`

   - **CMakeLists.txt**: Added src/platform/clock.cpp to smol_live and smol_replay targets

4. Errors and fixes:

   - **Initial CycleTimer first-cycle bug**: `_initialized` flag became true after first BeginCycle, but `_prev_tick_us=0` gave spurious `TickDtUs = _tick_us` (absolute tick). Fixed by switching to `_cycle_count >= 2` counter pattern initially, then later simplified to no-guard after AdvanceSyntheticCycle fix.

   - **Clock::ElapsedMs cache miscomprehension**: User moved `snapshot_send_time_ms = Clock::ElapsedMs()` to later in Step thinking it would give a later timestamp. I flagged that Clock caches via Update() so both reads return identical values. Also flagged user forgot to update `_prev_snapshot_send_time_ms`.

   - **CycleBusyUs under-reporting regression** (found in /cp-review): Moving BeginCycle after ReadSensors to fix native first-cycle dt=0 caused CycleBusyUs to miss 2-4ms sensor-read time on live hardware. User agreed: "we shouldn't be modifying flight loop to accommodate one hal's situation, especially for the native case, which never will actually fly on a vehicle." Fixed by introducing `hal::clock::AdvanceSyntheticCycle()` and moving BeginCycle back to top of Step.

   - **User rejected fallback pattern**: "no fallbacks. I deleted kflightloopintervalsec." I removed `measured_dt_sec > 0.0f ? measured_dt_sec : kFlightLoopIntervalSec` by making dt always non-zero via AdvanceSyntheticCycle.

   - **User rejected ClearTestOverride dead code** (found in /cadre:slop): Removed unused ClearTestOverride function.

   - **User rejected inheritance approach**: Pushed back on inheritance, user conceded: "Okay, I concede that inheritance isn't the right tool. But we should split up clock into two classes."

   - **sed multi-line limitation**: Single-line sed didn't match multi-line ComputeFailsafeResponse calls. Used `perl -i -0pe` with multi-line regex to strip `0.01f,` from all test call sites.

   - **jinja2 module missing**: Initial `python3 protocol/generate.py` failed. Fixed by `source ~/.venvs/smol/bin/activate`.

5. Problem Solving:
   - Solved: Altitude naming inconsistency (producer mislabeled field as MSL while storing NED-origin-relative value)
   - Solved: sqrt performance in 100Hz hot path via squared comparison
   - Solved: cycle_us semantics (absolute time vs duration) via delta computation; type change float32→uint32
   - Solved: Clock class confusion via split into Clock (current time) + CycleTimer (per-cycle state) + hal::clock contract
   - Solved: First-cycle dt=0 on native non-replay via AdvanceSyntheticCycle HAL function
   - Solved: CycleBusyUs under-reporting by moving cycle_count++ out of ReadImu side-effect
   - Solved: Wire-format lockstep via protocol/generate.py regeneration

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

   - `LoiterController` vs `dubins::PathManager` (loiter-only legs have `path.valid=false`)

   - SlowLoopBuildFn + void* context pattern (replaces file-scope singleton)
   - Test-first development (user explicitly corrected me on this)
   - No `std::function` (heap allocation concern for embedded)

# Code Review

Review all changes on the current branch against main.

## Process

### 1. Gather Changes

```bash
git diff main --name-only
```

If no changes, inform the user and stop.

For each changed file, read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand context. Also run:

```bash
git diff main
```

### 2. Review Against Guidelines

#### Code Reads Like Prose
- Descriptive function and variable names — no abbreviations that require mental decoding
- Linear data flows — can you read top-to-bottom without jumping around?
- Efficient line count — no bloat, no unnecessary abstractions
- DRY — is anything duplicated that shouldn't be?
- Single responsibility — each function does ONE thing, each class has ONE purpose
- Testable — could you write a test for this without mocking half the system?

#### Make Invalid States Unrepresentable
- Constraints encoded in types, not runtime checks
- No scattered validation for the same invariant
- `std::optional`, enums, and constructors used to enforce validity

#### Trace the Data
- Where does each value come from? What constraints does it carry?
- Are there redundant conversions or unnecessary intermediates?
- Does every downstream consumer get what it expects?

#### Always Make It Better
- Did we touch code without improving it?
- Are there obvious improvements just outside the diff boundary? (note in suggestions, don't block)

#### Project Conventions (from CLAUDE.md)
- No docstrings unless asked
- No fallbacks — code works or fails loudly
- No dead code, no commented-out experiments
- No default arguments
- Leading underscores for class data members
- PascalCase functions, snake_case locals, kCamelCase constants
- "latest" not "last" for most recent values
- Parameter passing: pointer for mutation, const ref for read-only, const value for scalars

### 3. Check For Slop
- Comments that explain "what" instead of "why"
- Defensive checks for conditions that can't happen
- Unnecessary try/catch or error handling beyond system boundaries
- Verbose logging that doesn't match existing patterns
- Style inconsistencies with surrounding code

### 4. Present Results

```
## Review Summary

**Assessment**: [APPROVE / REQUEST CHANGES]

### Positive Findings
- What was done well

### Required Changes
- Issues that must be fixed (file:line references)

### Suggestions
- Optional improvements

### Convention Violations
- Any CLAUDE.md or guideline violations
```

Be specific with file:line references. Prioritize correctness and readability over micro-optimizations. If approved, suggest running `/validate-smol` next.


ARGUMENTS: Look at all the code that has changed from main.

---

---

---

       static uint64_t TicksSinceInit();
       inline static uint64_t _init_tick_us = 0;
       inline static uint64_t _init_wall_us = 0;
       inline static double _utc_ref_sec = 0.0;

     - Reimplemented NowUs/NowMs/NowSec to flow through TicksSinceInit
     ```cpp
     void Clock::Init() {
       hal::clock::Init();
       _init_tick_us = hal::clock::NowTickUs();
       _init_wall_us = hal::clock::NowWallUs();
       _utc_valid = false;
       _utc_ref_sec = 0.0;
       _utc_ref_tick_us = 0;
       _test_override_enabled = false;
     }
     
     uint64_t Clock::TicksSinceInit() {
       if (_test_override_enabled) {
         return _test_now_us;
       }
       return hal::clock::NowTickUs() - _init_tick_us;
     }
     
     uint32_t Clock::NowUs() { return static_cast<uint32_t>(TicksSinceInit()); }
     uint32_t Clock::NowMs() { return static_cast<uint32_t>(TicksSinceInit() / 1000ULL); }
     float Clock::NowSec() { return static_cast<float>(TicksSinceInit()) * 1e-6f; }
     ```

   - **src/platform/watchdog.h** (edit)
     - Added wraparound invariant documentation

     - `1e6f` → `1e6` for replay time precision (double literal avoids float 7-digit precision loss after 1000s)
     ```cpp
     uint64_t NowTickUs() {
       return static_cast<uint64_t>(_rx.imu.time_sec * 1e6);
     }
     ```

     - EvaluateSlowLoopResponse now uses optional sentinel

     - snapshot.cycle_duration_us set post-BuildSnapshot
     ```cpp
     void FlightLoop::EvaluateSlowLoopResponse(const uint32_t current_elapsed_ms, const FlightMode mode,
                                               const bool airborne) {
       if (SlowLoopOk(current_elapsed_ms)) {
         _stale_since_ms.reset();
         _slow_loop_stale_triggered = false;
         return;
       }
       if (!_stale_since_ms) {
         _stale_since_ms = current_elapsed_ms;
       }
       if (mode != FlightMode::kAutonomous || !airborne) { return; }
       const uint32_t hold_ms = _have_primary ? kSlowLoopHoldMs : kSlowLoopBootstrapHoldMs;
       if ((current_elapsed_ms - *_stale_since_ms) > hold_ms) {
         _slow_loop_stale_triggered = true;
       }
     }
     ```

   - **src/protocol/snapshot_pack.h** (edit)
     - Removed cycle_duration_us parameter from PackTiming signature (caller now assigns post-pack)

   - **test/test_platform/test_platform.cpp** (new tests)
     - `ClockNowDerivations.NowMsAgreesWithUint64DivideAcrossWrap` — injects 2^32+1000 µs, asserts NowMs divides 64-bit-first
     - `ClockNowDerivations.InitDropsUtcAnchor` — sets UTC, re-Inits, asserts HasUtc()=false and UtcSec()=0.0

   - **test/test_slow_loop_response/test_slow_loop_response.cpp** (new test)
     - `SlowLoopResponseTest.StaleTimerLatchesEvenAtTickZero` — triggers stale at t=0, asserts trigger at exactly kHoldMs+1

Here are my comments about our PR:
For all files: There are a lot of comments. These violate the code-writing-guidelines. I understand that you might be leaving yourself notes for future phases. If that is the case, these comments need to be labeled as "[Notes for the Future]"

snapshot.h:
1. TimeMs()- Using the word "Time" in a function is completely ambiguous. What clock is this from? The time_sec parameter is also ambiguous. You need to stop using "time" as though it's obvious what time we're talking about.G

slow_loop_heartbeart.h: The comments are unnecessary. The ADRs hold the reasoning behind these values. We don't need to explain them in the code also.

safety_state.h: 
1. I'm assuming these comments will be removed at a later phase? If our code requires length comments like this, then our code is not clear enough. The comments can stay for now, if this file is a work-in-progress.
2. It seems like we should be wrapping the tier-1 parameters in a struct. The SafetyState class already has a lot of variables. If we decide to add more tiers, it will be get unruly. So either we decide that there will only ever be one tier (I'm open to the idea, if we discuss it), in which case, we could remove the FailsafeTier logic; or we plan for having muliple tiers at some point.

world_progress.h:
1. kMaxObjectives isn't used yet. What is it for? Do we need it now?
2. The file seems incomplete. TakeoffState and LandingState only have a single uint8_t, phase, and it's not defined what the value actually means. Is this just scaffolding? If so, it needs to be labeled as such. We shouldn't be passing of incomplete code as *complete*.

primary_control.h:
1. This class 100% duplicated the ControlOutput class.

skill_command.h:
1. We should be able to use ControlOutput instead of PrimaryControl.

clock_hal.h:
1. Why are all these comments necessary? It makes me think that our logic isn't obvious and functions aren't clearly named.
2. NowTickUs is not a good name. What is a "Tick"? What does this clock actually return?
3. NowWallUs is not a good name. "Wall" is meaningless. Is seems to be a monotonic timer. If so, it should be NowMonotonicUs. 

slow_loop_task.h:
1. Why are all these comments necessary? 

flight_loop.cpp:
1. timing.Lap(LoopTiming::kSnapshot) is called after the snapshot has been posted. Meaning each snapshot has the kSnapshot timing for the last step, not the current one. We either need to set the timing value manually, or kSnapshot from the timing struct.
2. This should be in its own function:
  if (nav && sensors) {
    // has_value() = kOk, nullopt = kNoData; richer driver-level status not
    // yet surfaced through the sample path.
    const SensorHealth health{
        .imu = SensorStatus::kOk,
        .gps = sensors->gps.has_value() ? SensorStatus::kOk : SensorStatus::kNoData,
        .mag = sensors->mag.has_value() ? SensorStatus::kOk : SensorStatus::kNoData,
        .baro = sensors->baro.has_value() ? SensorStatus::kOk : SensorStatus::kNoData,
    };
    const FlightSnapshot snapshot{
        .state = *nav,
        .sensors = health,
        .airspeed_mps = _latest_airspeed_ias.Get(kAirspeedSnapshotMaxAgeSec).value_or(0.0f),
        .mode = _active_mode,
        .current_elapsed_ms = current_elapsed_ms,
    };
    flight_snapshot_queue.push(snapshot);
  }
3. We now have a FlightSnapshot and a FlightLoopSnapshot, each of which are packed in the flight loop. So they're both essentially flight loop snapshots. If we added SensorHealth to FlightLoopSnapshot, then it would have everything that the slow loop required. So we could either take a subset of FlightLoopSnapshot to send to the slow loop, or we could send the whole thing and the slow loop would take what it needed from the FlightLoopSnapshot.
4. If you change _latest_skill_command to an optional, then _have_skill_command is unnecessary.
5. You need to rething the purpose of _latest_primary. It's essentially a fixed ControlOutput, right? We shouldn't make it some like some class is controlling the airplane intelligently. It's only purpose seems to be to hold the outputs at Idle. If there is another planned purpose, please let me know. 

cascade_controller.h:
1. two-letter variable abbreviations like "pc" are also unsatisfactory. make it more obvious. "primary_control" is clear, and not difficult to type or read.
2. the PrimaryControl branch n kAutonomous should be simplified, since we will likely be replacing PrimaryControl with ControlOutput (they are identical structs). So this branch could just return latest_primary.

1. Okay, I see your point for keeping them separate. Then only a naming change for FlightSnapshot is required. In order to know what to name it, I need to better understand how it's being used. It's really difficult to track what's happening in the slow loop, because of how the main_ functions work. The fact that the slow loop and the flight loop (fast loop) don't operate in a similar manner is confusing. I don't understand why we can't use a common pattern. We have flight_loop.cpp and background.cpp in the "core" directory, but the slow_loop_task.cpp is in "hal", and slow_loop.cpp is in "mission". The code is spread out all over the place. It's very difficult to track. I think we need to pause, plan, and refactor how we organize the core1 activities.

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

# Code Review

Review all changes on the current branch against main.

## Process

### 1. Gather Changes

```bash
git diff main --name-only
```

If no changes, inform the user and stop.

For each changed file, read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand context. Also run:

```bash
git diff main
```

### 2. Review Against Guidelines

#### Code Reads Like Prose
- Descriptive function and variable names — no abbreviations that require mental decoding
- Linear data flows — can you read top-to-bottom without jumping around?
- Efficient line count — no bloat, no unnecessary abstractions
- DRY — is anything duplicated that shouldn't be?
- Single responsibility — each function does ONE thing, each class has ONE purpose
- Testable — could you write a test for this without mocking half the system?

#### Make Invalid States Unrepresentable
- Constraints encoded in types, not runtime checks
- No scattered validation for the same invariant
- `std::optional`, enums, and constructors used to enforce validity

#### Trace the Data
- Where does each value come from? What constraints does it carry?
- Are there redundant conversions or unnecessary intermediates?
- Does every downstream consumer get what it expects?

#### Always Make It Better
- Did we touch code without improving it?
- Are there obvious improvements just outside the diff boundary? (note in suggestions, don't block)

#### Project Conventions (from CLAUDE.md)
- No docstrings unless asked
- No fallbacks — code works or fails loudly
- No dead code, no commented-out experiments
- No default arguments
- Leading underscores for class data members
- PascalCase functions, snake_case locals, kCamelCase constants
- "latest" not "last" for most recent values
- Parameter passing: pointer for mutation, const ref for read-only, const value for scalars

### 3. Check For Slop
- Comments that explain "what" instead of "why"
- Defensive checks for conditions that can't happen
- Unnecessary try/catch or error handling beyond system boundaries
- Verbose logging that doesn't match existing patterns
- Style inconsistencies with surrounding code

### 4. Present Results

```
## Review Summary

**Assessment**: [APPROVE / REQUEST CHANGES]

### Positive Findings
- What was done well

### Required Changes
- Issues that must be fixed (file:line references)

### Suggestions
- Optional improvements

### Convention Violations
- Any CLAUDE.md or guideline violations
```

Be specific with file:line references. Prioritize correctness and readability over micro-optimizations. If approved, suggest running `/validate-smol` next.

        const PlannedLeg& planned = *latest_planned_leg;

              .line_gain = params::Get<ParamIndex::kNavLineGain>(),
              .orbit_gain = params::Get<ParamIndex::kNavOrbitGain>(),
              .max_correction_deg = params::Get<ParamIndex::kNavMaxCorrDeg>(),

# Validate smol

Run all automated checks for the smol flight controller. Activate `~/.venvs/smol` before every command.

**CRITICAL**: Capture the FULL output of every command. Never re-run a command just to see which tests failed — read the output you already have. Use `2>&1` to merge stderr, and save long outputs to a file if needed.

## Checks

Run these in order. If a check fails, stop and report — do not continue to later checks.

### 1. Regenerate and format

Regenerate all generated files and run the formatter. This ensures we never commit stale generated code or unformatted source.

```bash
python3 protocol/generate.py && just format && just check-format && just check-codegen && just check-include-boundary
```

All four checks must pass. Generated files (`src/protocol/`) are excluded from formatting — the generator owns their style. `check-include-boundary` enforces ADR-C C-1 (fast-loop paths must not include from `src/mission/`).

### 2. Native unit tests

```bash
just test-native 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-native.txt
```

Read the FULL output to find failures. Do NOT re-run just to see which tests failed.

Report pass/fail count from the summary line (e.g., "118 test cases: 118 succeeded").

Known flaky: `test_smol_matches_full_after_full_sequence` (BUG-006, FullEkf nondeterminism). If ONLY this test fails, re-run once. If it fails twice, report it.

### 3. Thread sanitizer

```bash
just test-tsan 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-tsan.txt
```

Catches data races in SharedState, ring buffer, and cross-thread communication. Requires `setarch -R` for ASLR compatibility on Linux 6.x.

### 4. Elixir GCS tests

```bash
just test-gcs 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-gcs.txt
```

### 5. Native build

```bash
just build-native
```

### 6. RP2350B build (CMake)

```bash
just build-fc3
```

This catches missing source files in `CMakeLists.txt` and RP2350B-specific compilation errors that native builds miss.

### 7. Replay validation

```bash
just test-replay 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-replay.txt
```

This builds `native_full_ekf`, replays reference flight data through both EKFs, and checks RMS error bounds vs truth. Requires steps 4-5 to have passed.

## Report

```
## Validation Report

### Regenerate + format + include-boundary
[PASS — tree clean / PASS — N files updated / FAIL — details]

### Native tests
[PASS — N test cases: N succeeded / FAIL — details]

### Thread sanitizer
[PASS / FAIL — details]

### GCS tests
[PASS — N tests: N passed / FAIL — details]

### Native build
[PASS / FAIL]

### RP2350B build
[PASS / FAIL — details if failed]

### Replay validation
[PASS — N passed / FAIL — details]

### Summary
[READY TO SHIP / NEEDS FIXES — list what failed]
```

## Next Steps

- All pass: `/ship` to commit
- Failures: fix and re-run `/validate-smol`
