# Ship PR

Create a feature branch from the current branch, commit all changes, push, and open a PR.

## Pre-flight

Verify we have changes to ship:

```bash
git status
git diff --stat
git diff --cached --stat
```

If there are no changes (staged or unstaged, tracked or untracked), stop and inform the user.

## Gather Context

```bash
git branch --show-current
git log --oneline -5
```

The current branch becomes the PR's **base branch** (the branch to merge into). If already on a feature branch, ask the user if they want to PR into the branch they branched from instead.

## Steps

### 1. Determine branch name and commit message

If the user provided arguments, use them to derive:
- **Branch name**: kebab-case, prefixed with `feat/`, `fix/`, or `refactor/` based on the change type. Max 50 chars.
- **Commit message**: conventional commit format from the same description.

If no arguments provided, analyze the diff to determine both:
- Read `git diff` and `git diff --cached` and any untracked files
- Classify the change (feat, fix, refactor, docs, test, chore)
- Draft a branch name and commit message

**Show the user the proposed branch name and commit message before proceeding.** Wait for approval.

### 2. Create branch and commit

```bash
git checkout -b <branch-name>
```

Stage all relevant files. **Do NOT stage:**
- `.env` files or credentials
- Large binary files unless they're clearly intentional (e.g., `.uf2` firmware)

```bash
git add <specific files>
git commit -m "<message>

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>"
```

Use a HEREDOC for multi-line commit messages.

### 3. Push

```bash
git push -u origin <branch-name>
```

### 4. Create PR

```bash
gh pr create --base <base-branch> --title "<title>" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Summary
<1-3 bullet points describing the changes>

## Test plan
<How the changes were validated>


🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)
EOF
)"
```

The PR body should summarize what changed and how it was tested. Reference any validation output if `/validate-smol` or similar was run.

### 5. Report

```
PR created: <url>
Branch: <branch-name> → <base-branch>
```

## Safety Rules

- **Never force push**
- **Never push to main/master directly** — always create a branch
- **Always show the branch name and commit message before creating them**
- **If the user is already on a feature branch with commits**, ask whether to create a new branch or use the current one
- Stage files explicitly — never use `git add -A` or `git add .`

   - Challenge `const PlannedLeg& planned = *latest_planned_leg;` as a suspected copy (user was mistaken — it's a reference bind).
   - Challenge `NowUs` / `NowMonotonicUs` naming as uninformative — both clocks are monotonic, the distinction doesn't capture source.
   - Reject the whole clock architecture as smelly ("This architecture doesn't make sense... replay, SIL, and native need completely different types of clocks").
   - "Let's consult one our agents" — dispatched firmware-lead for HAL redesign recommendation.
   - Approve auto-mode implementation of the Clock HAL redesign.
   - Fix the awkward call site `hal::clock::HardwareClock<hal::clock::kHasHardwareClock>::NowUs()` with a free function.
   - Second `/cp-review` on the Clock HAL changes.
   - `/validate-smol` full validation suite.
   - "yes, fix it. we shouldn't ship bugs" — fix the pre-existing TSan race on `cycle_count`.
   - `/ship-pr` — commit, push, open PR.
   - "Option a, approved" — bundle all three commits (PR #77 cleanup + plan doc + Clock HAL redesign) into one PR against main.
   - Ask whether to compact before proceeding with Phase 1 of the Core 1 refactor.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - HAL capability-trait pattern: per-HAL `clock_caps.h` + explicit template specialization + include-path priority (no build-system -D flags, no #ifdef chains)
   - C++17 `if constexpr` name-lookup rules: (a) in non-template contexts, discarded branches are fully checked for name lookup; (b) in template contexts, non-dependent qualified names are still checked at template-definition time
   - Traits specialization with forward-declared primary (no body) + exactly one explicit specialization per build: each HAL ships the specialization matching its `kHasHardwareClock`
   - Wire-format zero-as-absent marker (decoder filter is OK) vs live-API zero-sentinel (fallback smell — rejected)
   - C++ reference binding from `std::optional<T>` dereference: `*opt` returns `T&`, binding to `const T&` is zero-cost
   - `std::atomic<T>` with `memory_order_relaxed` for monotonic counters (no cross-thread ordering dependencies)
   - TSan requires `setarch -R` on Linux 6.x for ASLR compat
   - PlatformIO include-path ordering: `-I src/hal/native` prepended before `-I src` so bare `#include "clock_caps.h"` resolves to the per-HAL file
   - Bundled-PR workflow when changes are tonally similar
   - ADR-F: slow-loop staleness threshold (150ms), heartbeat produced only by decision-tick task
   - Topology B: two Core-1 tasks (SlowLoop decision + IoService I/O), unified through `hal::SpawnCoreTask`

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - `src/hal/clock_hal.h` — HAL contract, rewritten
     ```cpp
     #pragma once
     #include <cstdint>
     namespace hal::clock {
     void Init();
     void AdvanceSyntheticCycle();
     uint64_t NowUs();
     template <bool HasHardwareClock>
     struct HardwareClock;
     }  // namespace hal::clock
     #include "clock_caps.h"
     namespace hal::clock {
     inline uint32_t HardwareNowUs() {
       return HardwareClock<kHasHardwareClock>::NowUs();
     }
     }
     ```

   - `src/hal/native/clock_caps.h` — NEW
     ```cpp
     #pragma once
     #include <cstdint>
     namespace hal::clock {
     inline constexpr bool kHasHardwareClock = false;
     template <>
     struct HardwareClock<false> {
       static uint32_t NowUs() { return 0u; }
     };
     }
     ```

   - `src/hal/rp2350b/clock_caps.h` — NEW
     ```cpp
     #pragma once
     #include <cstdint>
     namespace hal::clock {
     inline constexpr bool kHasHardwareClock = true;
     uint64_t NowHardwareUs();
     template <>
     struct HardwareClock<true> {
       static uint32_t NowUs() { return static_cast<uint32_t>(NowHardwareUs()); }
     };
     }
     ```

   - `src/hal/native/hal_native.cpp` — removed `NowWallUs() { return 0; }`, atomicized `cycle_count`:
     ```cpp
     #include <atomic>
     // ...
     // Written by fast loop (main thread) in AdvanceSyntheticCycle, read by the
     // slow loop thread via Clock::NowMs. Atomic because the read/write races.
     static std::atomic<uint32_t> cycle_count{0};
     // ...
     void AdvanceSyntheticCycle() {
       if (!replay_mode) { cycle_count.fetch_add(1, std::memory_order_relaxed); }
     }
     uint64_t NowUs() {
       if (replay_mode) { ... return 0; }
       return static_cast<uint64_t>(cycle_count.load(std::memory_order_relaxed)) * kCycleBudgetUs;
     }
     // Init: cycle_count.store(0, std::memory_order_relaxed);
     ```

   - `src/hal/native/hal_native_sil.cpp` — removed `NowWallUs() { return 0; }` stub.

   - `src/hal/rp2350b/hal_rp2350b_live.cpp` — renamed `NowWallUs()` → `NowHardwareUs()`. Body: `return to_us_since_boot(get_absolute_time());`

   - `src/hal/rp2350b/hal_rp2350b_replay.cpp` — renamed `NowWallUs()` → `NowHardwareUs()`. Same body.

   - `src/platform/clock.h` — removed `NowMonotonicUs()` declaration and `_init_monotonic_us` field. Now only flight-timeline + UTC concerns.

   - `src/platform/clock.cpp` — removed `NowMonotonicUs()` definition and `_init_monotonic_us` tracking.

   - `src/platform/cycle_timer.h` — rewritten to use traits:
     ```cpp
     void BeginCycle() {
       hal::clock::AdvanceSyntheticCycle();
       _prev_tick_us = _tick_us;
       _tick_us = Clock::NowUs();
       _cycle_start_hardware_us = hal::clock::HardwareNowUs();
     }
     uint32_t CycleBusyUs() const {
       return hal::clock::HardwareNowUs() - _cycle_start_hardware_us;
     }
     ```

   - `src/platform/lap_timer.h` — dropped `<bool Enabled>` template parameter; now plain class:
     ```cpp
     class LapTimer {
      public:
       void Start() { _last = hal::clock::HardwareNowUs(); }
       uint16_t Lap() {
         const uint32_t now = hal::clock::HardwareNowUs();
         const uint16_t elapsed = static_cast<uint16_t>(now - _last);
         _last = now;
         return elapsed;
       }
      private:
       uint32_t _last = 0;
     };
     ```

   - `src/diagnostics/loop_timing.h` — `LapTimer<true> timer;` → `LapTimer timer;`

   - `platformio.ini` — prepended `-I src/hal/native` to `[env:native]` and `[env:native_sil]` so `clock_caps.h` resolves to native variant.

   - `test/CMakeLists.txt` — prepended `${SMOL_ROOT}/src/hal/native` to `target_include_directories(smol_native PUBLIC ...)`.

   - `CLAUDE.md` — fixed `Clock::ElapsedMs()` → `Clock::NowMs()` in one code example.

   - `test/test_phase2_end_to_end/test_phase2_end_to_end.cpp:107` — comment fix: "cascade's monostate branch" → "Autonomous without a leg resolves to ControlOutput::Idle()".

   - `docs/superpowers/plans/2026-04-23-core-task-reorganization.md` — 216-line planning doc on disk (from prior commit ecc2be8b). Contains Phase 1-4 scope, exit criteria, gating conditions, topology B rationale, ADR impact summary. CANONICAL REFERENCE for Phase 1 work.

4. Errors and fixes:
   - **Slop command — stale `monostate branch` reference**: `test_phase2_end_to_end.cpp:107` still referenced the removed `std::variant` semantics. Fixed to "Autonomous without a leg resolves to ControlOutput::Idle()".
   - **Clock::NowHardwareUs template with default bool arg — name lookup failure**: First attempt put a `template <bool Enabled = kHasHardwareClock>` method in `Clock`. GCC error: `'NowHardwareUs' is not a member of 'hal::clock'`. Non-dependent qualified name checked at parse time regardless of template. Fix: removed `Clock::NowHardwareUs` entirely.
   - **Direct `if constexpr (kHasHardwareClock)` in `CycleTimer::CycleBusyUs()` — name lookup failure**: In a non-template function, discarded `if constexpr` branches are still checked for name lookup. GCC error same as above. Fix attempted: wrap in template helpers. Failed because `hal::clock::NowHardwareUs` is non-dependent even inside template bodies.
   - **Final fix — traits specialization with explicit per-HAL specialization**: Forward-declare `template <bool> struct HardwareClock;` (no body). Each HAL's clock_caps.h provides exactly ONE explicit specialization. Consumers write `HardwareClock<kHasHardwareClock>::NowUs()`. The native `<false>` body is `return 0u;` (never touches `NowHardwareUs`), so parse-time name lookup passes. On hardware, `<true>` body references `NowHardwareUs` which IS declared in the same file.
   - **Awkward call site**: `hal::clock::HardwareClock<hal::clock::kHasHardwareClock>::NowUs()` was unwieldy. User called it out. Added `inline uint32_t HardwareNowUs()` free function in clock_hal.h as sugar. Consumers now write `hal::clock::HardwareNowUs()`.
   - **TSan race on cycle_count (pre-existing on main)**: `static int cycle_count = 0;` written by main thread (AdvanceSyntheticCycle), read by slow-loop thread (NowUs → Clock::NowMs → SlowLoopInputBuilder::Build). Verified pre-existing by checking out main. User directive: "yes, fix it. we shouldn't ship bugs." Fix: `std::atomic<uint32_t> cycle_count{0}` with `fetch_add(1, relaxed)` / `load(relaxed)` / `store(0, relaxed)`.
   - **Stashed files restored during TSan baseline check**: `git stash && git checkout main -- . && ... && git checkout HEAD -- . && git stash pop` dance left `src/control/primary_control.h` and `test/test_primary_control/test_primary_control.cpp` staged as "new" — these should be DELETED on this branch (they live only on main). Fix: `git reset HEAD <files> && rm <files> && rmdir test/test_primary_control`.
   - **User feedback on compaction**: user asked "Should we do that first?" — I recommended yes, noting plan doc has everything Phase 1 needs.

5. Problem Solving:
   - Worked through three failed attempts at a compile-time-gated `NowHardwareUs` API before landing on the traits-class pattern with explicit per-HAL specialization. The key insight: C++17 `if constexpr` does NOT fully defer name lookup — non-dependent qualified names are checked at parse time even in discarded branches. The traits pattern sidesteps this by having each HAL ship exactly ONE complete specialization; no conditional compilation, no name-lookup hole.
   - Verified the race on `cycle_count` is pre-existing on main before attributing it to this branch, using a `git stash` + `git checkout main -- .` sequence (which later caused the stray-staged-files issue).
   - Decided (with user approval) to bundle three tonally-similar commits into one PR (path A) instead of splitting.
